## instr + strpos + to_hex Text-Alias Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **CRITICAL pre-existing-bug repair (two latent semantic divergences closed)**:
  - The `position` guard in `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` accepted short-name aliases `instr` and `strpos` but used SQL-standard `POSITION(substring IN string)` argument order (substring first). PostgreSQL/Oracle `instr(string, substring)` and `strpos(string, substring)` use the OPPOSITE ordering (string first). Any prior call to bare `instr` or `strpos` would have computed `haystack.find(needle)` with arguments swapped, returning wrong positions.
  - The `hex_encode`/`to_hex` guard in `data_scalar_functions_06_system_session_catalog.inc` accepted the short-name alias `to_hex` but routed through byte-encoding semantics via `HexEncodeBytes(RawBytesFromValue(...))`. PostgreSQL `to_hex(255) = 'ff'` (lowercase hex of the integer value, no leading zeros) is fundamentally different — byte-encoding of integer `255` would render as `"323535"` (ASCII hex of decimal string "255") rather than `"ff"`.
  - Both aliases removed from their respective guards; new dedicated guards added with correct semantics.
- **3 new canonical records**: `sb.scalar.instr` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7042 — 2-arg string-first), `sb.scalar.strpos` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7043 — 2-arg string-first PostgreSQL convention), `sb.scalar.to_hex` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7044 — PostgreSQL lowercase-hex integer convention, no leading zeros, zero-special-case returns `'0'`).
- **2 new engine guards**:
  - `instr`/`strpos` shared guard in `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` after the `position` guard: arity-2, null-strict, `string.find(substring)` with correct ordering, 1-indexed result, 0 when not found.
  - `to_hex` dedicated guard in `data_scalar_functions_06_system_session_catalog.inc` after the `hex_encode` guard: arity-1, null-strict, `ValueAsInt64Strict` extraction, cast int64 to uint64 via `static_cast` (twos-complement for negatives per PostgreSQL convention), zero-special-case returns `"0"`, else nibble-shift loop writes lowercase hex chars backwards into a 17-byte buffer.
- **2 pre-existing IdIs() narrowings**: position guard's IdIs dropped `"instr"`/`"strpos"` short-names; hex_encode guard's IdIs dropped `"to_hex"` short-name. Both narrowings are safe since no live fixture tests referenced the (incorrect) prior behavior — verified by repo grep across all SBSFC fixture corpora and test sources.
- **3 new SeedDef entries** binding canonicals to engine short_names `instr`/`strpos`/`to_hex` with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-011 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (35→38).
- **13 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-011 corpus 109→122: instr positive (`instr('hello world','world')=7` verifying corrected string-first ordering), instr not-found (`instr('hello','xyz')=0`), instr null_strict; strpos bare and signature-row positive/null coverage; strpos not-found; to_hex bare and signature-row positive/null coverage; to_hex zero edge.
- **5 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** in single lockstep batch via Python regex helper: `SBSQL-5A4A28A9E391 instr`, `SBSQL-E3C8DCA669D9 strpos`, `SBSQL-326152468215 strpos(string,substring)`, `SBSQL-BCD50600576E to_hex`, `SBSQL-DD35B99FD0EF to_hex(integer)`. **SBSQL-E50576CC5024 `instr(string,substring[,start[,occurrence]])`** remains `native_future` in the registry and remains required scope in the promotion matrix for a later Oracle-signature implementation slice; it was not promoted by this 2-arg sub-stream because the current engine guard does not implement start/occurrence semantics.
- **Selected static gates green after coordinator correction (2026-05-11T23:22:26Z).** Coverage advanced to `surfaces=2619 native_now=1794 native_future=790 cluster_private=35` after the `log` slice. ## add_months + last_day Temporal Arithmetic Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **2 new canonical records**: `sb.temporal.add_months` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7040 — 2-arg date+integer-month-offset; Oracle-convention day clamping when target month has fewer days than source) and `sb.temporal.last_day` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7041 — 1-arg returns the last day of the month containing the input). Both declare full oracle field set with detailed `return_type_rule`/`error_semantics` covering null-strict propagation, day-clamping behavior, and the first-day-of-next-month-minus-1 computation strategy.
- **2 new engine guards** in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` immediately after the week guard. **add_months** computes the target via signed total-months arithmetic (`total = y*12 + (mo-1) + months_offset`) using `new_y = total/12` and `new_mo = total%12 + 1` with explicit `new_y -= 1; new_mo += 12` adjustment when `total < 0 && total % 12 != 0` to protect against C++ negative-modulo behavior. Day clamps to a leap-aware `kDaysInMonth` array (February becomes 29 when `(y%4==0 && y%100!=0) || y%400==0`). Result formatted via `snprintf` `"%04lld-%02lld-%02lld"`. **last_day** computes first-day-of-next-month via `DaysFromCivil(next_y, next_mo, 1) - 1` then recovers the year/month/day via the `CivilFromDays` helper added in the prior isodow/week slice. Both guards extract input via `ValueAsText`, validate length, propagate null with `MakeNullValue("date")`, refuse with `RefuseFunctionInvalidInput` on bad input.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** binding canonicals to engine short_names `add_months`/`last_day` with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-012 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (23→25).
- **6 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-012 corpus 39→45: each canonical has positive + null_strict + 1 corner-case edge row. Corner cases verify Oracle-convention behavior: `add_months(2026-01-31|1) = 2026-02-28` (day-clamping in non-leap February); `last_day(2024-02-15) = 2024-02-29` (leap-year February recovery).
- **4 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** via Python regex helper in single lockstep batch: `SBSQL-712BEB777116 add_months` (bare), `SBSQL-1BA978245122 add_months(date|n)` (signature), `SBSQL-24D3CBDD3F18 last_day` (bare), `SBSQL-559A925B6DA8 last_day(date)` (signature). All canonical artifacts updated in lockstep.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T16:35:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1786 native_future=798 cluster_private=35`. Status-change authority gate `canonical=2619 errors=0` (thirty-second clean end-to-end exercise). SBSFC-012 fixture gate `45/25/0`. Full_oracle `207→211 (+4)`; round_trip_yes `193→197 (+4)`.
- **100-canonical-builtins milestone**: this slice crosses the 100-canonical-builtins threshold (98 → 100). Engine wiring now spans 7 packages: sb.scalar:72, sb.temporal:17, sb.session:5, sb.uuid:3, sb.regex:1, sb.json:2 — the temporal family at 17 wired canonicals reflects the sustained focus of recent slices (now/current_*, date_trunc, extract, make_date/time/timestamp/timestamptz, dow/doy/quarter, isodow/week, add_months/last_day).

## isodow + week ISO 8601 Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **New helper added**: `CivilFromDays(z, *y, *m, *d)` in `data_scalar_functions_02_string_regex.inc` as the inverse of the existing `DaysFromCivil(y, m, d)`. Both helpers implement Howard Hinnant's well-known calendar algorithms and form a closed pair — composing them is the identity. Pure functions, no system calls, valid over the same year domain as DaysFromCivil. Required by ISO 8601 week computation to recover the Thursday's year-of-week from its serial day count.
- **2 new canonical records**: `sb.temporal.isodow` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-703e — ISO 8601 Monday=1..Sunday=7, distinct from PostgreSQL's dow which uses Sunday=0..Saturday=6); `sb.temporal.week` (703f — ISO 8601 week number 1..53).
- **ExtractTimestampField extended** with 2 new field handlers: `isodow` via `(((days_from_civil % 7) + 10) % 7) + 1`; `week`/`isoweek` via the Thursday-of-same-ISO-week algorithm (compute iso_dow, move to Thursday, recover Thursday's year via `CivilFromDays`, then `(thursday_doy - 1) / 7 + 1`).
- **2 new engine guards** in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` immediately after the quarter guard; each dispatches to `ExtractTimestampField` with the corresponding fixed field name.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** binding canonicals to engine short_names with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-012 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (21→23).
- **4 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-012 corpus 35→39: each canonical positive on `2026-05-11` (verified against Python's `date.isocalendar()` returning `iso_year=2026 iso_week=20 iso_dow=1`) + null_strict.
- **4 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** via Python regex helper: `SBSQL-B92399F55F44 isodow`, `SBSQL-CA3A65D98456 isodow(date)`, `SBSQL-FBDA61BFAAD5 week`, `SBSQL-141F422A1427 week(date)`.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T16:15:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1782 native_future=802 cluster_private=35`. Status-change authority gate `canonical=2619 errors=0` (thirty-first clean end-to-end exercise). SBSFC-012 fixture gate `39/23/0`. Full_oracle `203→207 (+4)`; round_trip_yes `189→193 (+4)`.
- **Cumulative**: 109 surfaces promoted across 28 batches; 98 canonical builtins engine-wired across 7 packages (sb.scalar:72, sb.temporal:15, sb.session:5, sb.uuid:3, sb.regex:1, sb.json:2); 260 fixture rows across 3 corpora; 8 CTest gates; 0 outstanding divergences.

## dow/doy/quarter Temporal Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **3 new canonical records**: `sb.temporal.dow` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-703b — Sunday=0..Saturday=6 PostgreSQL convention), `sb.temporal.doy` (703c — 1..366 day-of-year), `sb.temporal.quarter` (703d — 1..4).
- **ExtractTimestampField helper extended** in `data_scalar_functions_02_string_regex.inc` with 3 new field handlers: `dow`/`day_of_week` via `((days_from_civil % 7) + 11) % 7` (offset 11 maps 1970-01-01 Thursday=4 correctly and handles C++ negative modulo behavior); `doy`/`day_of_year` via `DaysFromCivil(y, m, d) - DaysFromCivil(y, 1, 1) + 1`; `quarter`/`quarters` via `(month - 1) / 3 + 1`.
- **3 new engine guards** in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` immediately after the extract/date_part guard. Each takes a single temporal argument and dispatches to `ExtractTimestampField` with the corresponding fixed field name.
- **3 new SeedDef entries** binding canonicals to engine short_names with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-012 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (18→21).
- **6 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-012 corpus 29→35: each canonical has positive + null_strict. Positive cases use `2026-05-11` reference date with verified Python-computed expected values (dow=1 Monday; doy=131; quarter=2).
- **6 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** in single lockstep batch via improved Python regex helper: `SBSQL-3C2D518F0161 dow`, `SBSQL-F995EB3591B9 doy`, `SBSQL-A4AF5914BD3E quarter`, `SBSQL-30AC9D4B52DE dow(date)`, `SBSQL-A6B9F5E37598 doy(date)`, `SBSQL-FF788798B8C0 quarter(date)`.
- **Python helper improvement**: bulk-promotion regex updated to use a minimal-match `[^\n]*?` pattern anchored to line boundaries (`^...$` with `re.MULTILINE`). The prior `[^,]+` pattern failed on quoted-comma fields like `"dow(date)"` requiring manual Edit fallback. The new pattern handles all CSV row shapes uniformly. Note: when documenting regex patterns in narrative fields, avoid commas in character-class fragments since they break unquoted CSV cells (the heartbeat gate caught one such instance).
- **Heartbeat gate CSV-parsing issue caught**: prior narrative referenced the regex character class `[^,]+` literally in the AGENT_STATUS narrative which has an internal comma that broke CSV parsing. Replaced with `char-not-comma pattern` prose to avoid the literal comma. This is the second time the heartbeat gate caught a literal-comma-in-narrative issue (after the prior btrim slice's `btrim(text,chars)` literal); future narrative authors should use pipes or prose instead of literal commas inside parens.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T15:55:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1778 native_future=806 cluster_private=35`. ## cot/cotd Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

Both declare IEEE 754 infinity propagation at boundaries (multiples of pi for cot; multiples of 180 deg for cotd) rather than domain refusal, matching PostgreSQL semantics.

Both guards extract input via `ValueAsReal64`, propagate null, and return `MakeReal64Value` with IEEE 754 infinity at singularities.

## Degrees-Mode Trig Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **6 new canonical records**: `sb.scalar.sind` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7033), `sb.scalar.cosd` (7034), `sb.scalar.tand` (7035), `sb.scalar.asind` (7036), `sb.scalar.acosd` (7037), `sb.scalar.atand` (7038). Each declares full oracle field set including degree-based result ranges (forward variants unbounded; asind result `[-90, 90]`; acosd result `[0, 180]`; atand result exclusive `(-90, 90)`).
- **6 new engine guards** added to `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` after atan2 inside a single block scope `{ ... }` declaring `const double pi = std::acos(-1.0)` plus `deg_to_rad = pi/180.0` and `rad_to_deg = 180.0/pi` constants computed once per dispatch. The block-scope approach keeps the constants out of file scope and uses `std::acos(-1.0)` rather than `M_PI` macro reliance (M_PI is a POSIX extension, not C++ standard). Forward variants (sind/cosd/tand) extract input via `ValueAsReal64` then call `std::sin/cos/tan(input * deg_to_rad)`. Inverse variants (asind/acosd/atand) call `std::asin/acos/atan(input)` then scale by `rad_to_deg`. asind/acosd preserve the `|input| > 1` domain refusal via `RefuseFunctionNumericDomain`.
- **6 new SeedDef entries** binding the new canonicals to engine short_names `sind`/`cosd`/`tand`/`asind`/`acosd`/`atand` with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-010 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (33→39) with all 6 new canonicals.
- **14 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-010 corpus 94→108: forward variants (sind/cosd/tand) each have positive + null_strict = 2; inverse variants (asind/acosd: positive + domain_error + null_strict = 3 each; atand: positive + null_strict = 2 since unbounded domain).
- **6 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** in single lockstep batch via Python regex helper: `SBSQL-8F6D52F49E2F sind`, `SBSQL-F0D6A14F740B cosd`, `SBSQL-49A4ECEF0425 tand`, `SBSQL-8094575E89A8 asind`, `SBSQL-14E97EF6AED8 acosd`, `SBSQL-16A28BA0BC77 atand`. ## log2 + atan2 Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **2 new canonical records**: `sb.scalar.log2` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7031, domain restricted to input > 0 matching ln/log10), `sb.scalar.atan2` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7032, two-argument arctangent with result in [-π, π] including correct quadrant handling).
- **2 new engine guards** added to `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` after the hyperbolic guards. **log2** uses the same domain-checked UnaryReal pattern as ln/log10: extract via `ValueAsReal64`, refuse `SBSQL.NUMERIC.DOMAIN` if `input <= 0`, else delegate to `UnaryReal(std::log2)`. **atan2** is a dedicated binary guard: arity-2 check, null-strict across both args returning `MakeNullValue("real64")`, numeric-type validation via `ValueAsReal64` on both args, then `std::atan2(y, x)` returning `MakeReal64Value`.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** binding `sb.scalar.log2`/`atan2` to engine short_names `log2`/`atan2` with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.

The atan2 signature surface row required a manual Edit fallback for the status_matrix and backlog updates. Future bulk-promotion helpers should either escape quoted-comma fields or use proper CSV-aware parsing.

## Hyperbolic Trig Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

The exclusive (-1, 1) boundary refusal for atanh matches the canonical's spec exactly (engine could return ±infinity for atanh(±1) per std::atanh but the canonical chose strict boundary refusal).

## asin/acos/atan Inverse-Trig Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **Divergence closure**: `sb.scalar.asin` / `sb.scalar.acos` / `sb.scalar.atan` canonical records were added in SBSFC-010 second-pass (UUIDs 019dffbb-f001-7004 / 7005 / 7006) with `engine_entrypoint scalar_asin/acos/atan pending implementation std::asin/acos/atan available` notation in evidence_refs — engine impls were never added. This slice closes that 3-canonical divergence.
- **3 new engine guards** added to `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` immediately after the sin/cos/tan guards. **asin** and **acos** use dedicated guards with domain refusal: extract input via `ValueAsReal64`, check `|input| > 1.0`, refuse with `RefuseFunctionNumericDomain` if out-of-range; otherwise delegate to `UnaryReal(std::asin/acos)`. The domain refusal matches the canonical's `error_semantics` declaration ("domain error if absolute value of input greater than 1 must refuse with SBSQL.NUMERIC.DOMAIN"). **atan** uses simple `UnaryReal(std::atan)` since the canonical's `error_semantics` declares domain unbounded.
- **3 new SeedDef entries** binding `sb.scalar.asin`/`acos`/`atan` to the existing canonical UUIDs with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **3 canonical record evidence_refs updated**: replaced "pending implementation" notation with concrete engine reference + impl strategy (domain check then UnaryReal delegation for asin/acos; UnaryReal-only for atan).
- **SBSFC-010 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (22→25) with `sb.scalar.asin`/`acos`/`atan`.
- **8 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-010 corpus 67→75. Per canonical: asin (positive `asin(0)=0` + domain_error `asin(2)` + null_strict), acos (positive `acos(1)=0` + domain_error `acos(-2)` + null_strict), atan (positive `atan(0)=0` + null_strict — no domain_error case since atan accepts all real inputs).

## substr/greatest/least/nvl2 Canonical-Expansion + Engine-Impl Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **4 new canonical records**: `sb.scalar.substr` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7027 — alias of substring), `sb.scalar.greatest` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7028), `sb.scalar.least` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7029), `sb.scalar.nvl2` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-702a). Each declares full oracle field set with detailed return_type_rule and error_semantics.
- **2 new engine guards** added to `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` after the nullif guard. **greatest/least** uses a combined guard branching on `IdIs` for the comparator direction, with a unified-comparison strategy: try `ValueAsReal64` on every non-null arg; if all succeed → numeric comparison; otherwise → text comparison via `ValueAsText`. Nulls are skipped (PostgreSQL convention). All-null inputs return a typed null. The "best so far" tracking switches mode when transitioning from numeric to text comparison if a later arg fails numeric conversion. **nvl2** is a dedicated guard with arity-3 check, returning `request.arguments[2].value` when `arguments[0]` is null else `request.arguments[1].value`.
- **1 IdIs() extension** in `data_scalar_functions_03_uuid_crypto_bit.inc:198` adding `sb.scalar.substr` to the existing substring guard (which already accepts `substr`/`mid` bare-name aliases).
- **4 new SeedDef entries** binding `sb.scalar.substr` to engine short_name "substring", and `sb.scalar.greatest`/`sb.scalar.least`/`sb.scalar.nvl2` to their respective new engine short_names with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **SBSFC-011 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (31→35) with all 4 new canonicals. **NEW non_strict_null_handling exempt set** added — sb.scalar.greatest / sb.scalar.least / sb.scalar.nvl2 are exempt from the null_strict case_kind requirement because their semantics are skip-null (greatest/least) or null-test selector (nvl2) rather than null-propagation. Coverage of null behavior is exercised through positive_text fixtures that assert the documented non-strict result.
- **10 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-011 corpus 99→109. Substr: positive (substring extraction) + null_strict. Greatest: numeric comparison (3,1,5,2→5), text comparison (banana,apple,cherry→cherry), all_null (returns typed null via null_strict). Least: numeric comparison (3,1,5,2→1), skip-null (null,10,5→5), all_null. Nvl2: not-null (returns 2nd arg), is-null (returns 3rd arg, both as positive_text since the function returns a value not a null).
- **4 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B**: `SBSQL-55E29100DFED substr`, `SBSQL-4578A6991365 greatest`, `SBSQL-74FECCD28BBD least`, `SBSQL-83AB3A47F0D5 nvl2`. All canonical artifacts updated in lockstep.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T13:30:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1749 native_future=835 cluster_private=35`. Status-change authority gate `canonical=2619 errors=0` (twenty-fourth clean end-to-end exercise). SBSFC-011 fixture gate `109/34/0`. Full_oracle `172→178 (+6)`; round_trip_yes `156→160 (+4)`.

## Function Family Routing Extension + sb.json Wiring Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **CRITICAL latent-bug fix**: `IsDataScalarFunction` in `data_scalar_functions_03_uuid_crypto_bit.inc` only matched `data.scalar.`, `sb.fn.data.scalar.`, and `sb.scalar.` prefixes. But the SeedDefs added by prior SBSFC-012 / regex_match / uuid_v1_v7 sub-streams declared `family=data.scalar` for canonical ids in the `sb.temporal.`, `sb.session.`, `sb.uuid.`, `sb.regex.` namespaces — those function_ids would never have matched the family-routing check at runtime, falling through to the family-fallback refusal. The static fixture gates did not catch this because they only cross-check CSV structure against the canonical registry, not actual runtime dispatch routing. This slice extends `IsDataScalarFunction` to recognize all four additional sb.<package>. prefixes covering every previously-added canonical.
- **sb.json wiring (new package wired)**: `IsNoSqlDocumentFunction` in `nosql_document_functions.cpp` extended to recognize the `sb.json.` prefix. The existing JSON family already provides `JsonTypeOf` and `ExtractJsonObjectField` helpers in `nosql_document_functions.cpp`, so this sub-stream reuses them rather than reimplementing. 2 new IdIs entries added to `DispatchNoSqlDocumentFunction`: `sb.json.typeof` routes through the existing json_type guard; `sb.json.extract` routes through the existing json_get guard.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** for `sb.json.typeof` (UUID 019de5fc-2400-7d02-adb4-da4a6570dc6e, family=`nosql.document`, short_name `json_typeof`) and `sb.json.extract` (UUID 019de5fc-2400-7e24-878d-0b67cc0acc2f, family=`nosql.document`, short_name `json_extract`), both with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`. This is the first time canonicals in the sb.json namespace route through the nosql.document family rather than data.scalar.
- **2 canonical record updates** for sb.json.typeof and sb.json.extract: `error_semantics` tightened to specific arity refusal (1 for typeof, 2 for extract) + null-strict propagation; `return_type_rule` expanded to document the JsonTypeOf classifier behavior (text codepoint inspection of first non-whitespace char returning 'object'/'array'/'string'/'number'/'boolean'/'null') and ExtractJsonObjectField extraction semantics (returns null json_document if key not present); evidence_refs updated to point at the shared dispatch.
- **SBSFC-011 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (29→31) with `sb.json.typeof` and `sb.json.extract`. 5 new fixture rows extending SBSFC-011 corpus 94→99: `json_typeof-object` (`{"a":1}` → `'object'`), `json_typeof-array` (`[1,2,3]` → `'array'`), `json_typeof-null` (null_strict), `json_extract-present` (extract key `a` from `{"a":42}` → `42`), `json_extract-null` (null_strict). The fixture gate's seed-registry parser regex from the prior regex_match slice already recognized the sb.json prefix.
- **No SBSFC-009B promotions needed** — surfaces `SBSQL-83995B2BC266 json_extract` and `SBSQL-FE519C1C20F6 json_typeof` were already native_now from registry genesis. This is the fourth slice where the canonical was ahead of the engine (after make_timestamp, uuid_v1/v7, regexp_like); this slice closes the engine half.

## regex_match Engine Implementation Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **New canonical package wired**: sb.regex now has its first engine-wired canonical builtin. The slice closes a previously-undocumented engine-impl divergence — canonical surfaces `SBSQL-33900CA45C56 regexp_like` and `SBSQL-026D9D491FEE regexp_like(string,pattern[,flags])` were already `native_now` from registry genesis, but the engine had no regex implementation and the function_seed_registry.cpp comment from SBSFC-011 second-pass explicitly noted "regexp_like is deferred — canonical sb.regex.match record exists but no engine regex_match implementation yet". That deferral is now closed.
- **New engine guard** added to `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` immediately after the rpad guard. Implements `regexp_like(string, pattern[, flags])` using `std::regex` with ECMAScript syntax. Supports 2-arg (no flags) and 3-arg (flag string) forms. Optional flag character 'i' enables case-insensitive matching via `std::regex::icase`; any other flag character refuses with `SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT`. Invalid regex patterns caught via `std::regex_error` and refused with the same diagnostic. Null-strict across all args.
- **`#include <regex>`** added to `data_scalar_functions_00_common_helpers.inc` shared header (other engine files reach regex through this common include).
- **1 new SeedDef entry** for `sb.regex.match` (UUID 019de5fc-2400-76a3-9af7-b2ed28df4682, the existing canonical UUID) with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`. The prior "deferred" comment is replaced with an evidence note pointing to the new engine guard.
- **Canonical record updated**: `error_semantics` tightened from generic "arity/type/overflow/domain errors use builtin error compatibility matrix" to specific "arity must be 2 or 3 otherwise refuse with SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT; null-strict across all args; invalid regular expression pattern caught via std::regex_error and refused with SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT; unknown flag character refused". `return_type_rule` expanded to document ECMAScript syntax and 'i' flag handling. `evidence_refs` updated to point at the new engine guard.
- **SBSFC-011 fixture gate extended**: `target_canonicals` set extended (28→29) with `sb.regex.match`; seed-registry parser regex extended to recognize `sb.regex`, `sb.temporal`, `sb.session`, `sb.uuid`, `sb.json` prefixes (previously only `sb.scalar`, `sb.fn.`, `data.scalar`, `domain` — the parser-regex narrowing was a latent gap that this slice fixes since sb.regex.match needed to register as a known canonical).
- **6 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-011 corpus 88→94: `regexp_like-match` (`^hello` matches `'hello world'`), `regexp_like-nomatch` (`^world` does not match), `regexp_like-icase` (3-arg form with `'i'` flag), `regexp_like-null` (null_strict), `regexp_like-invalid` (domain_error for unclosed bracket `[unclosed`), `regexp_like-badflag` (domain_error for unknown flag `'z'`).
- **No SBSFC-009B promotions needed** — both regex surfaces were already native_now from registry genesis. This is the third slice where the canonical was ahead of the engine (after make_timestamp and uuid_v1/v7) where this slice closes the engine half.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T12:40:00Z).** Coverage unchanged at `surfaces=2619 native_now=1745 native_future=839 cluster_private=35`. Status-change authority gate `canonical=2619 errors=0` (twenty-second clean end-to-end exercise). SBSFC-011 fixture gate `94/28/0`. Full_oracle and round_trip_yes unchanged (engine-impl gaps not tracked by oracle or round-trip matrices).

## uuid_v1/v7 Engine Implementation Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **Divergence closure**: this slice closes a previously-undocumented spec-vs-impl divergence — canonical surfaces `SBSQL-BFDB58FD048D uuid_v1` and `SBSQL-F387AC0EFF32 uuid_v7` were already `native_now` from registry genesis, but the engine's uuid_generate dispatch refused all non-v4 invocations with "supports runtime fallback for compatibility UUID v4 only". This slice retroactively reconciles the engine implementation gap.
- **New engine helpers** added to `data_scalar_functions_01_numeric_temporal.inc`: `UuidBytesToCanonicalText(bytes)` (shared 16-byte → canonical hex-dash UUID formatter, also adopted by refactored `RandomUuidV4Text`); `RandomUuidV1Text()` (RFC 4122 v1 — 60-bit UUID-epoch timestamp via Unix-ns→100ns conversion with epoch offset 122192928000000000, random clock_seq, random node-id with multicast bit set per RFC 4122 to flag non-MAC origin); `RandomUuidV7Text()` (RFC 9562 v7 — 48-bit Unix millisecond timestamp + version 7 + 12-bit random rand_a + variant 10 + 62-bit random rand_b).
- **Engine dispatch extended** in `data_scalar_functions_07_dispatch_entrypoints.inc`: 2 new dedicated guards `sb.uuid.v1` and `sb.uuid.v7` (arity 0; deterministic_uuid_text override available; calls the respective helper); uuid_generate also extended to route version=1 and version=7 via the same helpers, then refuses any other version.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** for `sb.uuid.v1` (UUID 019de5fc-2400-7feb-b0a9-3353de7091ed) and `sb.uuid.v7` (UUID 019de5fc-2400-7fe3-a3d5-21174bd948db) with `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior`.
- **2 canonical record updates**: error_semantics tightened from generic "arity/type/overflow/domain errors use builtin error compatibility matrix" to specific "arity must be 0 otherwise refuse with SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT"; return_type_rule expanded to document RFC-compliant layout; evidence_refs updated to point at the new engine implementations.

## 2-Arg Trim Variants Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **New helper pattern**: `TrimChars(value, chars)` / `LTrimChars(value, chars)` / `RTrimChars(value, chars)` added to `data_scalar_functions_00_common_helpers.inc` after the existing whitespace-only helpers. Each searches `chars` via `std::string::find` for membership and erases matching chars from the appropriate end(s). Closes the previously-deferred btrim(text,chars) semantic gap and extends ltrim/rtrim/trim equivalently.
- **3 engine guards restructured** in `data_scalar_functions_03_uuid_crypto_bit.inc:116-118` from single-line `UnaryText(...)` calls into multi-arity branch guards. Each guard now: dispatches arity==1 through `UnaryText` (preserving 1-arg whitespace behavior unchanged); dispatches arity==2 through dedicated null-strict branch that calls `TrimChars`/`LTrimChars`/`RTrimChars`; refuses any other arity with `SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT`. The trim/btrim guard handles both canonicals; ltrim and rtrim guards remain dedicated.
- **4 canonical records updated** (sb.scalar.trim / sb.scalar.ltrim / sb.scalar.rtrim / sb.scalar.btrim). Each now declares a second overload signature (`trim(string,chars)` / `ltrim(text,chars)` / `rtrim(text,chars)` / `btrim(text,chars)`) and updated return_type_rule documenting chars-set semantics. error_semantics tightened from "UnaryText helper requires exactly one argument" to "arity must be 1 or 2 otherwise refuse with SBSQL.FUNCTION.INVALID_INPUT; null-strict across all args; 2-arg form removes any character present in the chars argument from both/left/right side". sb.scalar.btrim's "remains pending engine support" deferral note is removed since the 2-arg form is now supported.
- **3 native_future surfaces promoted via SBSFC-009B**: `SBSQL-234E59C1DF96 btrim(text[,chars])` + `SBSQL-185F244A9CA1 ltrim(text[,chars])` + `SBSQL-74418A7B7349 rtrim(text[,chars])`. The 4th surface `SBSQL-6C71783CA877 trim(text[,chars])` was already native_now from registry genesis (no status change needed); this slice retroactively reconciles the engine implementation gap for it as well.
- **8 new fixture rows** extending SBSFC-011 corpus 80→88 (canonical_builtins_covered unchanged at 27 since all 4 canonicals were already in the corpus from earlier slices). Coverage per canonical: positive chars-set form + null_strict for trim/btrim/ltrim/rtrim. Example: `trim('xxhelloxx', 'x') = 'hello'`; `ltrim('xyzhelloxyz', 'xyz') = 'helloxyz'`; `rtrim('xyzhelloxyz', 'xyz') = 'xyzhello'`; `btrim('abcabcfooabcabc', 'abc') = 'foo'`.

## lpad/rpad Text-Pad Engine Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **2 new canonical records**: `sb.scalar.lpad` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7023) + `sb.scalar.rpad` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7024). Each declares `lpad(text,length[,fill])` / `rpad(text,length[,fill])` overloads with cyclic-fill semantics (fill chars repeat to reach target length) and truncate-when-input-longer-than-length behavior. Length bounded to `[0, 1048576]` matching repeat's allocation cap. Default fill is single space when 2-arg form used.
- **2 new engine guards** added to `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` immediately after the repeat guard. Each guard handles both 2-arg (default fill=' ') and 3-arg (explicit fill) forms. Implementation details: null-strict across all args; arity refusal for <2 or >3; bounded-length refusal via `RefuseFunctionInvalidInput` for negative/over-cap lengths; empty-fill safeguard returns input unchanged when padding needed (cannot pad with zero-length fill); truncate-to-length when input ≥ target via `substr(0, target)`; pad loop uses cyclic indexing `fill[i % fill.size()]`.
- **2 new SeedDef entries** binding `sb.scalar.lpad`/`sb.scalar.rpad` to engine short_names `lpad`/`rpad` (data.scalar family) with FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior.
- **10 new fixture rows** (5 per canonical builtin) extending SBSFC-011 corpus 62→72. Each canonical covers: positive default-fill (`lpad(abc,5)='  abc'`), positive explicit-fill (`lpad(abc,5,xy)='xyabc'` per cyclic fill), positive truncate (`lpad(abcdef,3)='abc'`), null_strict, domain_error (negative length for lpad / over-cap length 1048577 for rpad). SBSFC-011 fixture gate target_canonicals 24→26.
- **4 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** in single lockstep batch: bare-name + signature variants for both lpad and rpad: `SBSQL-5086D5CE162D lpad`, `SBSQL-316F518F1992 lpad(text,length[,fill])`, `SBSQL-328A24D04BC5 rpad`, `SBSQL-436E400CDE00 rpad(text,length[,fill])`. Helper output: `registry=4 status_matrix=4 backlog=4 coverage_yaml=+4/-4`.
- **AGENT_STATUS heartbeat gate caught CSV parsing issue**: prior heartbeat row's `btrim(text,chars)` literal had an unescaped comma that the CSV parser interpreted as a field separator, corrupting downstream fields. Fixed by replacing comma-in-parens with pipe-in-parens (`btrim(text|chars)`). Convention now: `(text|chars)` instead of `(text,chars)` in agent narrative to keep CSV well-formed without quoting overhead.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (2026-05-11T11:00:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1738 native_future=846 cluster_private=35`. ## btrim Bare-Name Canonical Alias Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **New canonical record** `sb.scalar.btrim` (UUID 019dffbb-f001-7022) declares semantic equivalence to `sb.scalar.trim` for the **1-argument whitespace-only form**. sblr_binding/ast_binding/engine_entrypoint reference `scalar_trim` (shared dispatch via UnaryText+TrimAscii). evidence_refs notes the engine implementation lives at `data_scalar_functions_03_uuid_crypto_bit.inc:116` and IdIs already accepts `btrim` bare-name — this slice adds the canonical `sb.scalar.btrim` alias to the same IdIs list.
- **Conservative scope decision**: the **2-arg signature surface** `SBSQL-234E59C1DF96 btrim(text[,chars])` is **NOT promoted** by this slice. The engine's UnaryText helper enforces `arguments.size() == 1` and refuses any 2-arg invocation, so promoting the 2-arg surface would be a lie about engine capability. The 2-arg form remains native_future pending engine support for trim-with-chars semantics. error_semantics in the canonical record documents this scope explicitly.
- **1 new SeedDef** binding `sb.scalar.btrim` to engine short_name "trim" (data.scalar family) using FunctionImplementationState::implemented_behavior.

- **1 native_future surface promoted via SBSFC-009B**: `SBSQL-12FB359A9976 btrim` (bare-name). All canonical artifacts updated in lockstep.
- **Argument-order semantic concerns investigated and deferred** for instr/strpos (engine treats arg[0]=needle, arg[1]=haystack; postgres/oracle convention is opposite — arg[0]=haystack, arg[1]=needle), to_hex (engine encodes raw bytes via ValueAsText→bytes, not PostgreSQL's integer-to-hex semantic), and btrim 2-arg form (engine UnaryText is 1-arg only). All three blocked on engine work, not canonical-spec authority.

## Crypto Digest Refusal Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **First refusal-implemented slice — establishes new pattern** for canonical surfaces whose engine implementation is a known refusal pending a configuration dependency. The refusal IS the implemented behavior: parser admits the surface (status native_now, allowed_lowering yes), engine handles dispatch by returning a structured `SB_DIAG_FUNCTION_DEPENDENCY_UNAVAILABLE` diagnostic. Future surfaces with similar dependency-runtime-refusal semantics (e.g. configured-provider-required functions) reuse this pattern.
- **4 new canonical builtin records** added: `sb.scalar.md5/sha1/sha256/sha512` (UUIDs 019dffbb-f001-701d/701e/701f/7020). Each declares `security_policy: requires configured cryptographic digest provider; engine refuses at dispatch when no provider is configured` and `error_semantics: dependency-runtime-refusal — engine returns SBSQL.FUNCTION.DEPENDENCY_UNAVAILABLE (SB_DIAG_FUNCTION_DEPENDENCY_UNAVAILABLE) when no cryptographic provider is configured`. engine_entrypoint references the shared digest dispatch.
- **4 new SeedDef entries** using `FunctionImplementationState::implemented_policy_security_or_dependency_runtime_refusal` — first slice to use this state. Honest declaration that the implementation IS the structured refusal.
- **1 IdIs() extension** in `data_scalar_functions_07_dispatch_entrypoints.inc:72` adding `sb.scalar.md5/sha1/sha256/sha512` aliases. The dispatch then derives algorithm from id when called via canonical alias (vs deriving from arg[1] for bare `digest`). All non-fnv64 algorithms refuse with `RefuseFunctionWithDiagnostic(dependency_unavailable, SB_DIAG_FUNCTION_DEPENDENCY_UNAVAILABLE, ...)` per pre-existing engine code.
- **SBSFC-011 fixture gate extended**: new `dependency_unavailable` case_kind recognized (must declare expected_diagnostic_code, must not carry expected_result_value — same discipline as arity_error/domain_error/overflow/type_error); new `refusal_implemented` canonicals set exempts these builtins from the null_strict coverage requirement (engine refuses before reaching any null handling); dependency_unavailable case satisfies positive-coverage requirement (the refusal IS the implemented behavior).
- **4 new fixture rows** with `case_kind=dependency_unavailable` and `expected_diagnostic_code=SBSQL.FUNCTION.DEPENDENCY_UNAVAILABLE`. SBSFC-011 corpus 52→56; target_canonicals 17→21.
- **8 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B** in single lockstep batch: bare-name + (text|binary) variants of md5/sha1/sha256/sha512. Helper output: `registry=8 status_matrix=8 backlog=8 coverage_yaml=+8/-8`.

## overlay Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **New overlay engine guard** added to `data_scalar_functions_04_json_collection_range.inc` after replace. Implements SQL-standard `overlay(string PLACING substring FROM start [FOR length])` with 3-arg form (length defaults to substring's character length) and 4-arg form (explicit length). Null-strict across all args (returns null character). start must be ≥ 1 (one-based per SQL standard); start ≥ 0 refused with InvalidInput. length must be ≥ 0. If start_index ≥ source length, appends replacement to end. Otherwise replaces `min(length, source.size()-start_index)` characters starting at start_index with replacement.
- **1 new SeedDef entry** bound the pre-existing canonical UUID `019de5fc-2400-7390-9528-049a6e15ad82` (record existed since registry genesis; engine impl was the missing half).
- **4 new fixture rows** appended to SBSFC_011 corpus (44→48; canonical_builtins_covered 15→16): 3-arg `overlay(hello world, SBSQL, 7)=hello SBSQL` (length defaulted to 5 = strlen(SBSQL)); 4-arg `overlay(hello world, new, 7, 5)=hello new`; null_strict; arity_error for start=0.
- **2 native_future surfaces promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B**: `SBSQL-3C43316DB906 OVERLAY` (bare keyword surface) and `SBSQL-8FF76E4AA98A OVERLAY(textPLACINGtextFROMstart[FORlength])` (full-syntax surface).

## EXTRACT(EPOCHFROM) Sub-Stream Closure Evidence

- **`ExtractTimestampField` helper extended** in `data_scalar_functions_02_string_regex.inc` with a new `epoch`/`epochs` branch. Computes Unix seconds since 1970-01-01T00:00:00 UTC by parsing year/month/day/hour/minute/second components from the ISO-like timestamp text and calling a new `DaysFromCivil(y, m, d)` helper (Howard Hinnant's well-known days-from-civil algorithm). Days × 86400 + hour × 3600 + minute × 60 + second. Time component is optional — defaults to 00:00:00 for date-only inputs.
- **`DaysFromCivil` helper added** as a pure function above ExtractTimestampField. Pure proleptic Gregorian calendar formula, valid for `year` in [-(2^31), 2^31). No mutable state, no system calls, no dependency on locale or timezone (always UTC).
- **2 fixture rows** updated/added in SBSFC_012: `SBSFC012-date_part-epoch` (was the arity_error placeholder; now a positive_text case asserting `date_part('epoch', '2026-05-11T14:23:45')=1778509425`), `SBSFC012-extract-epoch` (covers the EXTRACT(EPOCHFROM...) surface via the shared sb.temporal.date_part dispatch with the same expected value). Both fixtures hand-verified: DaysFromCivil(2026,5,11)=20584; 20584×86400=1778457600; +14×3600+23×60+45=51825; total=1778509425 ✓.
- **1 native_future surface promoted to native_now via SBSFC-009B**: `SBSQL-17F632F80DD2 EXTRACT(EPOCHFROM...)`. Helper output: `registry=1 status_matrix=1 backlog=1 coverage_yaml=+1/-1`.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (validated 2026-05-11T08:00:00Z).** Coverage `surfaces=2619 native_now=1715 native_future=869 cluster_private=35`. Status-change authority gate `canonical=2619 errors=0` (ninth clean end-to-end exercise). SBSFC-012 fixture gate `25/14/0`. Round-trip matrix shows minor shift in `descriptor_oracle_pending=98→99 (+1)` because the EXTRACT(EPOCHFROM...) surface now full_oracle-matches via date_part but the oracle matrix counts only one canonical_name per surface; round_trip_yes itself unchanged at 126 since the underlying canonical was already wired in earlier SBSFC-012 third-pass.
- **No new canonical builtin record** added in this slice — the epoch case dispatches through the existing `sb.temporal.date_part` canonical record. `ExtractTimestampField` is an internal helper, not a separately-registered builtin.
- **Cumulative state**: 42 surfaces promoted across 9 batches; 48 canonical builtins engine-wired across 5 packages; 125 oracle-derived fixture rows across 3 fixture corpora; 8 CTest gates; 0 outstanding spec-vs-impl divergences. Native_now movement: 1673→1715 (+42). Round_trip_yes movement: 53→126 (+73).
- **Architecture invariant compliance**: pure helper extension (DaysFromCivil + epoch branch) + fixture authoring + status promotion only; no SBLR opcode added; no parser worker, server, listener, storage, MGA, or transaction-recovery file modified; no WAL surface introduced. `DaysFromCivil` is a deterministic pure function — bit-identical output for any given input. ## Spec-vs-Implementation Divergence Reconciliation Closure Evidence

- **All 5 accumulated spec-vs-impl divergences resolved** by tightening the engine to match canonical authority. Direction chosen: canonical spec is the source of truth, engine adjusted to emit the spec-mandated diagnostic codes and null-strict behavior. This preserves the canonical-authority discipline that drives the execution_plan and improves user-facing error specificity.
- **2 new diagnostic-specific refusal helpers added** to `project/src/engine/functions/common/function_result_helpers.{hpp,cpp}`: `RefuseFunctionNumericDomain` (emits `SB_DIAG_FUNCTION_NUMERIC_DOMAIN`) and `RefuseFunctionNumericDivisionByZero` (emits `SB_DIAG_FUNCTION_NUMERIC_DIVISION_BY_ZERO`). Both follow the existing `RefuseFunctionInvalidInput`/`RefuseFunctionOverflow` pattern wrapping `RefuseFunctionWithDiagnostic` with `SblrStatusCode::execution_failed`. Function-id/UUID/package fields auto-attached per existing pattern.
- **3 numeric engine guards tightened** in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc`: ln (line 84) and log10 (line 92) now use `RefuseFunctionNumericDomain` for the "input must be positive" case; mod (line 121) now uses `RefuseFunctionNumericDivisionByZero` for the "divisor must not be zero" case. Each refusal now surfaces a domain- or division-specific diagnostic id matching the canonical `error_semantics` field in `builtin-expression-registry.yaml`.
- **2 temporal engine guards rewritten** in `data_scalar_functions_06_system_session_catalog.inc` for `make_date` (line 39) and `make_time` (line 49). The old code combined the null check and the int64 type check in a single loop, causing null input to refuse with InvalidInput rather than propagating to null. The new code uses two separate loops: first iteration checks for null and returns `MakeFunctionSuccess(... MakeNullValue("date" or "time"))` on any null arg; second iteration checks for int64 type and refuses non-int64 args with InvalidInput. This makes the null-strict semantics match the canonical spec's `null_behavior=strict` declaration. `make_timestamp` at line 59 already had the correct dedicated null guard returning `MakeNullValue("timestamp")` — no change needed.
- **5 fixture notes updated** to reflect aligned state: `SBSFC010-ln-domain`, `SBSFC010-log10-domain`, `SBSFC010-mod-divzero`, `SBSFC012-make_date-null`, `SBSFC012-make_time-null` notes now describe the unified spec+engine behavior rather than flagging divergence. The fixture `expected_diagnostic_code` / `expected_result_value` fields were already correct — only the prose notes needed updating.
- **Selected SBSFC gates green (validated 2026-05-11T07:15:00Z).** Coverage gate: `surfaces=2619 native_now=1712 native_future=872 cluster_private=35` (unchanged — engine-helper edits, no status drift). No-stub gate: `files_scanned=21 findings=0`. Heartbeat validate: `agents=1 tracker_rows=36 declared_lanes=23 errors=0`. Status-change authority gate: `canonical=2619 errors=0`. Deterministic-generation/no-network gate: `passed generators=9 network_findings=0 determinism_findings=0`. SBSFC-010 fixture gate: `56/19/0`. SBSFC-011 fixture gate: `44/15/0`. SBSFC-012 fixture gate: `21/13/0`.
- **No status promotions**, no canonical-registry expansion, no SBLR opcode added — pure engine-side reconciliation. The reconciliation matters because (1) it eliminates a known spec-vs-impl drift backlog, (2) it improves end-user error specificity (consumers can distinguish domain errors from generic invalid-input), and (3) it removes 5 "follow-up patch needed" items from the next-coordinator-routing list.
- **Cumulative state after reconciliation patch.** 39 surfaces promoted across 7 batches; 47 canonical builtins engine-wired across 5 packages; 121 oracle-derived fixture rows across 3 fixture corpora; 8 CTest gates registered; **0 outstanding spec-vs-impl divergences**. Remaining engine implementation work: uuid_v1/v7 runtime generators, overlay, regex_match, bit_shift_*, EXTRACT(EPOCHFROM), make_timestamptz, arithmetic/comparison operator dispatch.
- **Architecture invariant compliance for this slice.** Engine helper additions + engine guard updates + fixture-note updates only; no SBLR opcode added; no parser worker, server, listener, storage, MGA, or transaction-recovery file modified; no WAL surface introduced. The two new helpers route through the same `RefuseFunctionWithDiagnostic` core that all other refusals use — diagnostics remain dispatched through the unified SBLR diagnostic vocabulary. MGA copy-on-write authority remains the sole transaction recovery model.

## SBSFC-010 Second-Pass Engine Wiring Closure Evidence

- **8 new canonical numeric builtins wired into the engine** via the same 3-surgical-edit pattern as the first pass. `project/src/engine/functions/registry/function_seed_registry.cpp` extended with 8 new `SeedDef` entries binding canonical ids to engine entrypoints under `(family="data.scalar", state=implemented_behavior, package=core)`: `sb.scalar.sin` (uuid 019dffbb-f001-7001-8a00-000000000001 → entrypoint `sin`), `sb.scalar.cos` (...7002 → `cos`), `sb.scalar.tan` (...7003 → `tan`), `sb.scalar.exp` (...7007 → `exp`), `sb.scalar.ln` (...7008 → `ln`), `sb.scalar.log10` (...7009 → `log10`), `sb.scalar.trunc` (...700a → `trunc`), `sb.scalar.mod` (...700b → `mod`). UUIDs sourced from the canonical-registry expansion numeric-batch-2 (the `019dffbb-f001-700x` family declared in `builtin-expression-registry.yaml`). `project/src/engine/functions/families/data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` extended the `IdIs()` matcher lists for `trunc`, `exp`, `ln`, `log10`, `sin`, `cos`, `tan`, `mod` to include their `sb.scalar.<name>` canonical aliases. The `data_scalar_functions_03_uuid_crypto_bit.inc::IsDataScalarFunction` admit guard already accepts the `sb.scalar.` prefix (added in first pass), so no additional change there. Existing implementations (`std::sin`/`std::cos`/`std::tan` via `UnaryReal()`, `std::exp` via `UnaryReal()`, `std::log` via `UnaryReal()` after dedicated null + non-positive guards, `std::log10` via `UnaryReal()` after dedicated null + non-positive guards, `std::trunc` via `UnaryReal()`, `std::fmod` after dedicated null + divisor-zero guards) are reused unchanged. `aliases-deferred`: `truncate` (engine treats as `trunc` alias but canonical-registry expansion did not yet add `sb.scalar.truncate`) and `log` (engine treats as `ln` alias but canonical dialect choice is pending) remain excluded from the canonical `sb.scalar.*` matcher lists.
- **21 new oracle-derived fixture rows appended to `SBSFC_010_NUMERIC_BUILTIN_FIXTURES.csv`** (corpus expanded from 22 to 43 rows). Coverage per new builtin: sin (positive sin(0)=0.0, null_strict); cos (positive cos(0)=1.0, null_strict); tan (positive tan(0)=0.0, null_strict — deliberately avoiding pi/2 because `UnaryReal()` rejects non-finite results with `RefuseFunctionOverflow`); exp (positive exp(0)=1.0, null_strict, overflow exp(1000) → SBSQL.NUMERIC.OVERFLOW); ln (positive ln(1)=0.0, null_strict, domain_error ln(-1) → SBSQL.NUMERIC.DOMAIN); log10 (positive log10(100)=2.0, null_strict, domain_error log10(-1) → SBSQL.NUMERIC.DOMAIN); trunc (positive trunc(1.7)=1.0, negative trunc(-1.7)=-1.0, null_strict); mod (positive mod(10,3)=1.0, null_strict on first arg, domain_error mod(10,0) → SBSQL.NUMERIC.DIVISION_BY_ZERO). Every new fixture row notes that the surface is currently native_future awaiting SBSFC-009B promotion before the row can carry e2e_passed evidence — the engine wiring lands now so the wire is hot the moment the status flip closes.
- **Spec-vs-implementation divergences captured in fixture notes for follow-up patch.** The canonical registry says `ln`/`log10` domain errors must refuse with `SBSQL.NUMERIC.DOMAIN` and `mod` divisor-zero must refuse with `SBSQL.NUMERIC.DIVISION_BY_ZERO`. The existing engine implementations use `RefuseFunctionInvalidInput(...)` instead, which maps to a different diagnostic code. Three fixtures (`SBSFC010-ln-domain`, `SBSFC010-log10-domain`, `SBSFC010-mod-divzero`) declare the canonical expectation; the CTest end-to-end probe will surface the divergence and a follow-up engine-side patch will either update the refusal helper or update the canonical spec. The static gate accepts these fixtures because case_kind discipline is independent of the actual emitted diagnostic code (gate enforces only that error-class case_kinds carry a diagnostic, never a result).
- **Fixture gate target set extended to 15 canonical builtins**. `sbsql_sbsfc_010_numeric_builtin_fixture_gate.py::target_canonicals` now requires positive-or-edge coverage AND null_strict coverage (except for volatility-volatile builtins like `sb.scalar.random`) for the original 7 plus the 8 second-pass builtins. Baseline run (2026-05-11T03:25:00Z): `sbsql_sbsfc_010_numeric_builtin_fixture_gate=passed fixtures=43 canonical_builtins_covered=15 errors=0`.
- **Selected prior gates remain green or correctly failing by design after the second-pass engine edits.** SBSFC-000 coverage gate: `surfaces=2619 native_now=1673 native_future=911 cluster_private=35` (no canonical surface drift). SBSFC-007 no-stub gate: `files_scanned=19 findings=0` (clean — new fixtures and gate update introduce no forbidden patterns). SBSFC-008 agent heartbeat validate: `agents=1 tracker_rows=36 declared_lanes=23 errors=0`. SBSFC-009B status-change authority gate: `canonical=2619 errors=0` (no status change in this second pass — the 8 newly-wired native_future surfaces remain native_future until SBSFC-009B is executed; the engine wiring is dormant for them and only activates on lowering once the status flip closes). SBSFC-009C deterministic-generation/no-network gate: `passed generators=9 network_findings=0 determinism_findings=0`.
- **Cumulative SBSFC-010 surface coverage after first pass + canonical expansion + second pass.** Engine has canonical `sb.scalar.*` bindings for: `abs`, `sqrt`, `power`, `ceil`, `floor`, `round`, `random`, `sin`, `cos`, `tan`, `exp`, `ln`, `log10`, `trunc`, `mod` (15 builtins). Direct surface coverage: ~30 surface_ids in the SBsql canonical registry now have engine-bound canonical authority (the 22 first-pass intersection_b + intersection_a rows once SBSFC-009B closes, plus the 8 second-pass native_future rows that become live on SBSFC-009B). 43 static fixture rows ready for CTest e2e probe authoring in a built environment.
- **Architecture invariant compliance for this slice.** Engine function registration only; no SBLR opcode added; no parser worker, server, listener, storage, MGA, or transaction-recovery file modified; no WAL surface introduced. All 8 newly-wired builtins are scalar functions invoked under an existing MGA transaction with no durability, recovery, or visibility semantics. The engine entrypoints reuse the existing `UnaryReal()` helper (which itself uses `MakeFunctionSuccess`/`MakeNullValue`/`RefuseFunctionOverflow`/`RefuseFunctionInvalidInput` dispatch surface) and the dedicated guards in `ln`/`log10`/`mod`. MGA copy-on-write authority remains the sole transaction recovery model.

## SBSFC-010 Canonical-Registry Expansion (Numeric Batch 2) Closure Evidence

- **12 new canonical builtin records appended to `public_contract_snapshot`.** Records added: `sb.scalar.sin`, `sb.scalar.cos`, `sb.scalar.tan` (engine implementations exist via `UnaryReal(std::sin/cos/tan)` in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc`); `sb.scalar.asin`, `sb.scalar.acos`, `sb.scalar.atan` (engine entrypoints pending implementation — declared canonically so SBSFC-010 second-pass authoring knows what to bind); `sb.scalar.exp`, `sb.scalar.ln`, `sb.scalar.log10` (engine implementations exist via `std::exp`/`std::log`/`std::log10`); `sb.scalar.trunc` (engine implementation exists via `std::trunc`); `sb.scalar.mod` (engine implementation exists via dedicated mod guard handling divisor-zero and INT64_MIN%-1); `sb.scalar.sign` (engine entrypoint pending implementation). Each record carries the full oracle field set required by SBSFC-004 for `full_oracle` classification: `builtin_id`, `builtin_uuid` (new UUIDv7 family `019dffbb-f001-7XXX-*` to mark canonical-expansion vintage), `kind=scalar`, `canonical_name`, `package=sb.core`, `status=accepted`, `syntax_forms`, `overloads` with `argument_rule=descriptor_authoritative`, `return_type_rule`, `coercion_rule`, `null_behavior`, `collation_charset_rule`, `timezone_rule`, `volatility=immutable`, `determinism`, `side_effects=none`, `sblr_binding=sblr.expr.scalar_<name>.v3`, `ast_binding=ast.expr.scalar_<name>`, `engine_entrypoint=scalar_<name>`, `optimizer_properties` (foldable + index_eligible + generated_column_eligible + cost_class=cpu_scalar), `security_policy`, `donor_rendering`, `error_semantics` (name-specific: domain refusals for asin/acos/ln/log10, overflow refusal for exp, division-by-zero and INT64_MIN%-1 for mod, total over finite reals for trunc/sin/cos/tan/atan/sign with non-finite propagation per IEEE 754), `conformance_cases` (BIF-CONF-9d3c8a72f00x family), and `evidence_refs` citing the canonical-registry-expansion vintage and (for implemented entrypoints) the exact engine implementation site.
- **Three surfaces deliberately excluded from this batch pending coordinator decision on alias handling.** `log` (SBSQL-B6FABD092548), `log(numeric)` (SBSQL-07E8D99F156F), and `truncate` (SBSQL-BD47F88ED308) remain `pending_canonical_authority_entry`. The engine treats `log` as an alias for `ln` and `truncate` as an alias for `trunc` (per the existing `IdIs()` lists in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc`), but the canonical SBsql semantics for `log` are dialect-dependent (Postgres: log = log10; Oracle: log(base,x); standard SQL: log = ln). The SBSFC-004 oracle matcher matches by `canonical_name` and does not consult a donor/alias table, so adding a `sb.scalar.log` record now would prematurely commit a dialect choice. Coordinator decision required before unblocking these 3 rows.

All 9 generators in the SBSFC-009C deterministic-generation gate report identical md5 pre/post-regeneration including the regenerated `FUNCTION_SEMANTIC_ORACLE_MATRIX` (new md5 `9762996fb9f3eaed3eede0c85d63cb3c`) and the regenerated `SBLR_BINARY_ROUND_TRIP_MATRIX` (new md5 `7b17a2d5c67c7fdd3f28089dd730df49`).

No-stub gate: `files_scanned=19 findings=0`. Heartbeat validate: `agents=1 tracker_rows=36 declared_lanes=23 errors=0`. Status-change authority gate: `canonical=2619 errors=0`. These can be wired identically to the SBSFC-010 first-pass pattern: extend `function_seed_registry.cpp` with `SeedDef` entries binding `sb.scalar.<name>` to `("data.scalar", "<name>", implemented_behavior, core)`; extend the `IdIs()` matcher lists in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` for each name; author fixture rows; register a static fixture gate. The remaining 8 surfaces (asin × 2, acos × 2, atan × 2, sign × 2) need new engine entrypoints first (the underlying `std::asin`/`std::acos`/`std::atan`/`std::copysign` calls exist in the C++ standard library but no current engine guard wraps them). All work landed in this slice is canonical-spec-only — no engine, parser worker, server, listener, storage, MGA, or transaction-recovery file modified; no WAL surface introduced.

## SBSFC-010 First-Pass Planning Evidence

- **Oracle matcher fix landed.** The `normalize_name()` function in `project/tools/sb_parser_gen/generate_function_semantic_oracle_matrix.py` was extended to recognize the canonical `sb.<package>.<name>` builtin id format and extract the leaf name, so surface rows whose `canonical_name` is the engine-anchored builtin id (`sb.scalar.abs`, `sb.temporal.now`, etc.) now match against the leaf form in `builtin-expression-registry.yaml`. After re-running the SBSFC-004 oracle generator and the SBSFC-006 / SBSFC-009A downstream generators, the oracle matrix now reports `full_oracle=99` (+32), `binding_only=108` (+50), `pending_canonical_authority_entry=1367` (-82). The round-trip matrix reports `round_trip_yes=85` (+32), `round_trip_yes_descriptor_oracle_pending=98` (+50), `blocked_until_canonical_oracle_entry=1490` (-82).
- **SBSFC-010 first-pass target identified.** The intersection of SBSFC-003 ownership=`function_numeric_worker` (3 native_future rows) and SBSFC-004 oracle_authority_status=`full_oracle` (limited to numeric canonical names: abs, sqrt, power, ceil, floor, round, random) yields 22 unique surface_ids covering 7 canonical numeric builtins. The full target list is in `artifacts/SBSFC_010_FIRST_PASS_TARGET_ROWS.csv`. 19 rows are already native_now (intersection_b — no status change required). 3 rows are native_future (intersection_a — require NF_TO_NN_PROMOTE via SBSFC-009B before status change closes).
- **Engine implementation survey.** The existing scalar function tree at `project/src/engine/functions/families/` carries math implementations in `data_scalar_functions_05_conversion_conditional.inc` (lines 60/63/66/77/108): `std::ceil`, `std::floor`, `std::round`, `std::sqrt`, `std::pow` invoked via the `UnaryReal()` helper. These implementations exist but are not registered under the canonical function ids (`sb.scalar.ceil`, etc.) declared in `builtin-expression-registry.yaml`. The grep for the canonical engine entrypoint names (`scalar_abs`, `scalar_sqrt`, etc.) returns no matches — those entrypoint names are aspirational identifiers from the oracle authority that the C++ engine has not yet exposed. `scalar_abs` and `scalar_random` have no `std::abs`/`std::rand` matches in the function tree either.
- **Remaining work required to close the 22 target rows to `e2e_passed`:** (1) define the canonical function entrypoints `scalar_abs`, `scalar_sqrt`, `scalar_power`, `scalar_ceil`, `scalar_floor`, `scalar_round`, `scalar_random` in `project/src/engine/functions/families/` and bind them to the canonical builtin ids `sb.scalar.abs`, `sb.scalar.sqrt`, etc. via the function registry seed; (2) wire the SBLR opcode dispatcher to map `sblr.expr.scalar_abs.v3` etc. through to those entrypoints; (3) ensure the SBsql worker's lowering layer in `project/src/parsers/sbsql_worker/lowering/` maps the bound-AST for the surface canonical names (`abs`, `abs(x)`, `abs(numeric)`, `sb.scalar.abs`) to the canonical SBLR envelope; (4) author 22 per-row CTest fixture YAMLs covering positive cases (e.g., `abs(-5) == 5`), negative cases (e.g., arity mismatch), null behavior, overflow/domain edges, and volatility/determinism assertions for `random`; (5) configure CMake to discover the fixtures and run them; (6) execute CTest in a build environment to confirm pass; (7) update PER_ROW_EVIDENCE_MANIFEST.csv to transition the 22 rows from `final_state=pending` to `final_state=e2e_passed` with timestamps; (8) for the 3 native_future rows, execute SBSFC-009B status-change authority gate to perform the NF_TO_NN_PROMOTE transition in lockstep across canonical CSV ledgers, coverage YAML, MANIFEST, generated registry, and inventory.
- **Architecture-invariant compliance for this planning step:** read-only intersection analysis plus oracle-matcher fix plus downstream regeneration; no transaction model touched; no engine, parser worker, server, listener, storage, or MGA file modified yet; no WAL surface introduced. MGA copy-on-write authority remains the sole transaction recovery model. The implementation routing decision is escalated to the coordinator.

## SBSFC-009E Closure Evidence

- `artifacts/FAILURE_TRIAGE_TAXONOMY.csv` regenerated: 14 categories — the 12 required by SBSFC-009E acceptance (parser, binder, sblr, server, engine, fixture, oracle, auth, mga, catalog, driver, generation) plus two operationally necessary extras (cluster_profile for SBSFC-025 routing; agent_stall for the SBSFC-008 heartbeat system). All 8 columns populated with zero blanks: `failure_category`, `owner_lane`, `diagnostic_code_prefix`, `required_evidence`, `standard_action`, `escalation_path`, `failure_id_prefix`, `notes`.
- Each row carries a `diagnostic_code_prefix` field that binds the failure class to the canonical diagnostic vocabulary: parser → `SBSQL.SYNTAX.*;SBSQL.LEXER.*;SBSQL.CST.*`; binder → `SBSQL.BINDING.*;CATALOG.NAME.NOT_FOUND_OR_NOT_VISIBLE`; sblr → `SBLR.ENVELOPE.*;SBLR.OPCODE.*;SBLR.VERIFIER.*`; server → `SERVER.ADMISSION.*;SBPS.*`; engine → `ENGINE.EXEC.*;ENGINE.API.*;SBLR.DISPATCH.*`; mga → `MGA.VISIBILITY.*;MGA.TRANSACTION.*;MGA.RECOVERY.*`; etc. This provides the dispatch authority that triage gates use to route failures to the correct owner.
- The `mga` row's `standard_action` field explicitly forbids WAL/redo-log behavior as a repair: `fix_mga_behavior_under_copy_on_write_authority_no_wal_no_redo_log_recovery_path`. Its `notes` field reinforces: "WAL/redo-log behavior is never an acceptable repair; the project's architecture invariant forbids WAL."
- `failure_id_prefix` field provides a stable per-category namespace for FAILURE_INVENTORY.csv rows. `agent_stall` uses `stall` to match the existing inventory format produced by the SBSFC-008 `detect-stalls` subcommand; other categories use `fail-<category>` (e.g., `fail-parser`, `fail-sblr`, `fail-mga`).
- `escalation_path` field records the worker-to-coordinator escalation route for each category, so triage decisions are deterministic and the coordinator knows where to look when a failure crosses lanes.
- Generator script: `project/tools/sb_parser_gen/generate_failure_triage_taxonomy.py`. Deterministic; idempotent (md5 `ca754f672695d4f74dc73903cdea8df8` stable). Cluster_private rows refuse at lower in the public build with SBSQL.SURFACE.NOT_ADMITTED + SBSQL.CLUSTER.AUTHORITY_REQUIRED — no public binary envelope, no public dispatch path.
- The forbidden_authority_sources field is uniform across all 2619 rows (single distinct value), embedding the execution_plan rule that SQL text, identifier names, parser branch names, donor command names, and operation-family-only routing are never execution authority. The round-trip gate must reject any envelope whose dispatch attempts to use one of these.
- The execution_authority_model field declares `mga_copy_on_write;no_wal_authority` for every row; audit count zero rows lack the declaration. The matrix is the authoritative per-row record that MGA copy-on-write is the only transaction execution authority for accepted dispatch.
- Generator script: `project/tools/sb_parser_gen/generate_sblr_binary_round_trip_matrix.py`. Inputs are repo-local (canonical surface registry CSV + the SBSFC-004 oracle matrix CSV); no network access; deterministic. Two consecutive runs produce identical output (md5 `93215794d3ae5597e02fc4eff55473bf`).

The MGA/no-WAL invariant is now baked into both `mga_execution_authority` (SBSFC-005) and `execution_authority_model` (SBSFC-006) at the per-row level, providing two machine-readable assertions per surface.

- `artifacts/FUNCTION_SEMANTIC_ORACLE_MATRIX.csv` generated: 1574 rows (1555 functions + 18 operators + 1 variable), zero duplicates, perfect intersection with the expression-runtime surface set in the canonical surface registry. All 33 columns populated with zero blanks.
- `oracle_authority_status` distribution: `full_oracle=67` (rows where canonical `builtin-expression-registry.yaml` provides volatility, determinism, side_effects, null_behavior, collation_charset_rule, timezone_rule, return_type_rule, coercion_rule, error_semantics, optimizer_properties, security_policy, donor_rendering, syntax_forms, conformance_cases, sblr_binding, ast_binding, engine_entrypoint); `binding_only=58` (rows that match `builtin-sblr-expression-binding.yaml` by builtin_id and inherit only sblr_binding and engine_entrypoint — semantic fields remain `oracle_pending`); `pending_canonical_authority_entry=1449` (no canonical authority entry matched; all oracle fields are `oracle_pending`). 67 + 58 + 1449 = 1574.
- Match policy: surface canonical_name is normalized (lowercase, stripped from first `(`, punctuation removed; for pure-punctuation operators like `@` and `@@` the original lowercased name is preserved). Expression-registry match is by normalized canonical_name; binding-registry match is by builtin_id derived from normalized name with known package prefixes (sb.scalar, sb.temporal, sb.uuid, sb.session, sb.aggregate, sb.window, sb.special_form, sb.operator, sb.json, sb.regex). Oracle values are sourced exclusively from canonical authority — never from implementation output.
- Coordinator scope decision (option a per SBSFC-004 entry): rows whose oracle is missing from canonical authority are emitted with `oracle_pending` placeholders rather than fabricated values. P2 implementation slices may not implement a row whose `oracle_authority_status` is `binding_only` or `pending_canonical_authority_entry` until canonical authority is extended (or the row is routed to `remove_by_spec_change` via SBSFC-009B). This is recorded as a current blocker for the execution_plan: canonical builtin-expression-registry.yaml expansion is the gating activity that unblocks P2 row-level work for 1449 functions.
- Sample full_oracle rows verify the matrix carries real oracle data: `SBSQL-00439AD179E6 POSITION(substringINtext)` → volatility=immutable, side_effects=none, null_behavior=strict, sblr_binding=`sblr.expr.scalar_position.v3`, engine_entrypoint=`scalar_position`; `SBSQL-026D9D491FEE regexp_like(string,pattern[,flags])` → volatility=`immutable_locale_versioned`, sblr_binding=`sblr.expr.regex_match.v3`, engine_entrypoint=`regex_match`.
- Generator script: `project/tools/sb_parser_gen/generate_function_semantic_oracle_matrix.py`. Inputs are repo-local (canonical surface registry CSV + two canonical YAML registries); no network access; deterministic. Two consecutive runs produce identical output (md5 `17d64ff63b84ff623c33d04a20cdf2dd`).
- Prior gates and generators remain green: SBSFC-000 coverage gate passes; SBSFC-001 strict ledger generator idempotent; SBSFC-003 promotion matrix generator idempotent. SBSFC-002 no-grey gate continues to fail by design (correct).
- Architecture invariant compliance for this slice: read-only YAML/CSV consumption; no transaction model touched; no engine, parser worker, server, listener, storage, or MGA file modified; no WAL surface introduced. The oracle matrix is a contract-derived expectation record only.

## SBSFC-002 Closure Evidence

## Resume Procedure

1. Read `TRACKER.csv`, `ACCEPTANCE_GATES.csv`, and this file.
2. Confirm no active agent owns the next write scope in `artifacts/AGENT_STATUS.csv`.
3. Run the last validation command if one is recorded.
4. If validation fails, classify the failure using `artifacts/FAILURE_TRIAGE_TAXONOMY.csv`.
5. Update this file with the next command before spawning or assigning work.

## Active Coordination - 2026-05-12T13:24Z

- Coordinator completed the `SBSFC-021` SBWP/TLS COPY ingestion slice and reconciled the COPY wire drift found by read-only agent `019e1c3c-ef76-7780-8464-dc2ccd08d539`.
- Implementation correction: SBWP `CopyInResponse` now uses the native-wire/driver-authority message id `0x51`, while client `CopyData`, `CopyDone`, and `CopyFail` remain `0x0D`, `0x0E`, and `0x0F`. The worker emits a 5-byte `CopyInResponse` payload (`format_profile=0x00`, `window_bytes`) matching the existing driver parsers. The TLS smoke now asserts the id and payload profile.
- COPY execution route: `COPY ... FROM STDIN` over SBWP/TLS now requires negotiated `kFeatureStreaming`, buffers newline-delimited `canonical_row_fields_text` rows from `CopyData`, converts them to canonical `row_field` / `row_null_field` SBLR operands, and executes `dml.execute_import_rows` on `CopyDone` through the server/engine public ABI under the active engine MGA transaction. The parser does not commit, roll back, execute donor SQL, or claim persistence authority.
- Negative evidence added: unnegotiated `CopyData` fails closed with `SBWP.FEATURE.NOT_NEGOTIATED`; malformed row-field payload after a valid copy initiation fails with `SBSQL.COPY.DATA_ROW_INVALID` and preserves active transaction state for rollback.
